## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the restoring force has nonlinear dependence on position x, and may include time-dependent driving or parametric excitation terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Extended Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (quintic nonlinear restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (linear oscillator with sinusoidal driving)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Driven Duffing with cosine: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * abs(x) (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric potential)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general polynomial restoring force)
- Driven with quadratic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (general driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force from pendulum dynamics)
- Damped driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (phase-shifted driving)
- Rational restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) (bounded nonlinear restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power polynomial restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium
- Even-power terms (x²) in restoring force break symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms additive to position-dependent terms
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative coupling between x and trigonometric functions of t
- Sinusoidal position dependence sin(c*x) indicates a periodic potential (e.g., pendulum-type systems)
- Absence of velocity variable suggests acceleration depends only on conservative forces and external driving
- Cubic nonlinearity x³ with opposite sign to linear term indicates hardening/softening spring behavior
- If time t appears only inside trigonometric functions, the system has a periodic external force
- Rational functions of x suggest bounded restoring forces that saturate at large displacements
